COLI EHEC - AUSTRIA: O146, UNKNOWN SOURCE\n********************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Fri 26 Feb 2021\nSource: Food Safety News [edited]\nhttps://www.foodsafetynews.com/2021/02/investigators-still-looking-for-source-of-outbreak-of-e-coli-infections-in-austria/\n\n\nAustrian authorities are investigating an outbreak of Shiga toxin-producing _E. coli_ [also called enterohemorrhagic _E. coli_ (EHEC)] infections that has affected a handful of people. Between September and December 2020, 6 people fell ill with infections from _E. coli_ O146:H28. Those sick live in 5 federal states. Two people needed hospital treatment. As yet, there is no indication as to the source of the outbreak, according to the Austrian Agency for Health and Food Safety (AGES). It is understood other countries in Europe have not reported related infections.\n\nThe Federal Ministry of Social Affairs, Health, Care and Consumer Protection (BMSGPK) has instructed AGES to investigate the outbreak with the relevant state authorities. Austrian food testing in 2018 found _E. coli_ O146 in 3 samples of fresh game meat and one sample of fermented sausage. In 2017, 4 isolates were typed as _E. coli_ O146 from 2 samples of raw meat from wild ruminants, fresh bovine meat and a fermented sausage.\n\nThe latest Zoonoses Report from the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) and European Centre for Disease Prevention and Control (ECDC) shows _E. coli_ O146 was the 5th most frequent serogroup reported in confirmed human infections in 2018.\n\nAnyone who has developed symptoms of EHEC infection should seek medical attention and tell their doctor about their possible exposure to the bacteria. Specific tests are required to diagnose the infections, which can mimic other illnesses. The symptoms of _E. coli_ infections vary for each person but often include severe stomach cramps and diarrhea, which is often bloody. Most patients recover within 5 to 7 days. Others can develop severe or life-threatening symptoms and complications, according to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC).\n\nAbout 5% to 10% of those diagnosed with EHEC infections develop a potentially life-threatening kidney failure complication, known as a hemolytic uremic syndrome (HUS). Symptoms of HUS include fever, abdominal pain, feeling very tired, decreased frequency of urination, small unexplained bruises or bleeding, and pallor.\n\nMany people with HUS recover within a few weeks, but some suffer permanent injuries or death. This condition can occur among people of any age but is most common in children younger than 5 years old because of their immature immune systems, older adults because of deteriorating immune systems, and people with compromised immune systems such as cancer patients. People who experience HUS symptoms should immediately seek emergency medical care. People with HUS will likely be hospitalized because the condition can cause other serious and ongoing problems such as hypertension, chronic kidney disease, brain damage, and neurologic problems.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This Shiga toxin-producing O146 is one of the non-O157 serotypes causing enterohemorrhagic _E. coli_ disease. The source of this zoonotic infection in Austria is not clear at this point. Potential vehicles for transmission include salads, unpasteurized dairy products and undercooked ground beef. - Mod.LL\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map:\nAustria: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/109]\nSee Also\n2020\n----\nE. coli EHEC - Viet Nam: (YB) RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=7444580", "date": "2020-06-10 15:02:50", "main_text": "UNKNOWN NEMATODE - VIET NAM: (YEN BAI) REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n**************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Sun 7 Jun 2020 09:43 ICT\nSource: Saigon Giai Phong (SGGP) [edited]\nhttps://sggpnews.org.vn/health/young-man-in-northern-region-infested-with-dracunculus-medinensis-87070.html\n\n\nThe National Hospital for Tropical Diseases in Hanoi announced the admission in hospital of a young man in the Northern Province of Yen Bai who was infested with a rare worm.\n\nThe 23-year-old man was hospitalized when he was suffering abscesses on his legs and then the abscesses spread to his arms. Additionally, he had fatigue and pain for many days.\n\nSurgeons later have removed 5 rare intestinal worms with a length of 30-60 centimeters [12-24 in] from the abscesses in his hands.\n\nHead of the hospital's Surgery Ward Dr Tran Thuong Viet said the worm had never been discovered in Viet Nam before but is commonly found in rural areas of Africa with scientific name _Dracunculus medinensis_ -- a species of roundworm that causes Guinea worm disease.\n\nThere is no specific medication [for the disease caused by this worm], doctors have used the usual dose to remove the worms.\n\nThrough investigation, doctors found that the man usually eats living fish and crabs. As the worm is rare in the country, physicians said that it is necessary to study water sources where the man lives because the worm eggs are spread via a water source.\n\n[Byline: Nguyen Quoc; translation: Uyen Phuong]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[It is highly unlikely that this case is due to the Guinea worm _Dracunculus medinensis_. Guinea worm has never be described outside Africa. Transmission is by drinking water contaminated with small copepods or eating raw fish. Recently dogs have been identified as hosts as well (https://www.cdc.gov/dpdx/dracunculiasis/index.html).\n\nIf this is indeed _D. medinensis_, it will be the 1st time the parasite has been reported outside of Africa. With an incubation time of up to 18 months this means contamination in the environment and probably more human cases.\n\nIt is strongly advised that the material removed from the patients is sent for molecular analysis. - Mod.EP\n\nA number of tissue nematodes and larva migrans syndromes, some associated with consuming aquatic animals, can be found in Southeast Asia. Histopathology and DNA analysis of the recovered worms will be key to determining whether this case is a unusual manifestation of a previously reported parasitic nematode, or in fact a novel parasitic infection. - Mod.LXL\n\nHealthMap/ProMED map of Viet Nam: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/66860]\n\n.................................................sb/ep/mj/lxl", "reports": [{"diseases": ["unknown"], "syndromes": [], "event_date": [], "locations": [{"location": "Hanoi", "country": "Vietnam"}, {"location": "Viet Nam", "country": "Vietnam"}, {"location": "Saigon", "country": "Vietnam"}, {"location": "the Northern Province", "country": "South Africa"}, {"location": "Guinea", "country": "Guinea"}]}]}, {"archive_id": "6744567", "headline": "PRO/EDR> Community-acq. pneumonia - USA: (WV) school-aged children, unknown etiology, RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=6744567", "date": "2019-10-24 18:00:21", "main_text": "COMMUNITY-ACQUIRED PNEUMONIA - USA: (WEST VIRGINIA) SCHOOL-AGED CHILDREN, UNKNOWN ETIOLOGY, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n*******************************************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Tue 22 Oct 2019\nSource: The Intelligencer [edited]\nhttps://www.theintelligencer.net/news/top-headlines/2019/10/pneumonia-outbreak-reported-in-marshall-county-schools/\n\n\nApproximately 50 cases of pneumonia are being reported among children in Marshall County Schools, according to officials today [22 Oct 2019]. \"Cameron Elementary School and Hilltop Elementary School have a high percentage of reported cases,\" said Shelby Haines, superintendent of schools. The outbreak, though, isn't limited to those 2 schools.\n\n\"There are around 50 reported cases,\" said Thomas Cook, Marshall County Health Department administrator. The majority of cases are occurring \"in a couple of schools,\" he said, but added, this illness \"is not just confined to Marshall County.\n\nThere are other cases of this throughout the state,\" said Tony Wood, spokesman for Marshall County Schools.\n\nIt has yet to be determined whether the cases of pneumonia are caused by a virus or bacteria, Cook said. State epidemiologists are sending testing kits to the health department for distribution to rapid care facilities, Cook said. Swabs taken from patients will be sent to the West Virginia Bureau of Public Health for testing and diagnosis of the form of infection affecting local residents.\n\nTreating the symptoms is recommended for either form of pneumonia. Antibiotics, however, are prescribed only for bacterial pneumonia. Doctors \"are not going to give antibiotics unless you have a bacteria that you want to eradicate,\" Cook explained.\n\nExtensive cleaning is being done in school buildings to prevent additional cases. \"Last week [week of 14 Oct 2019], we began getting phone calls of reported cases of illness in a number of schools,\" Haines said. \"When those reports came, we began cleaning with an approved disinfectant to try to get a jump on it. We increased the custodial staff to clean with approved methods. \"The superintendent said the school district has bought its own ionizer, a machine that is being used for cleaning during after-school hours. \"In the evening, we run a cleaning device that sprays disinfectant on all surfaces, on top of regular cleaning. It sprays a mist and sticks to surfaces,\" she said.\n\nIn addition, school personnel and health educators are training children on the importance of hand washing, using facial tissues. and coughing into one's elbow. \"Hand washing is the key to everything,\" Cook said.\n\nThe health department has sent a sanitarian to Cameron and Hilltop schools to check the facilities. \"The county (school system) has really been pro-active in cleaning and education,\" the health administrator said.\n\nWhen the outbreak began, \"we started to receive calls from the parents, from the urgent care (centers) with people coming in with some difficulty breathing, wheezing, lethargy, fever. Chest X-rays were showing congestion in lungs and classical signs of pneumonia,\" Cook said.\n\nThe health official predicted that pneumonia also will affect the adult population and younger children. Patients can go back to school or work when their fever subsides for 24 hours without the use of fever-reducing medication, he said.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[We are told that about 50 cases of pneumonia are being reported among children, mainly in 2 elementary schools in the Wheeling, West Virginia Metropolitan Statistical Area, Marshall County, West Virginia, although additional cases are also being reported throughout the state. Patients are said to be school children with difficulty breathing, wheezing, lethargy, fever, and chest X-rays findings consistent with pneumonia. No further details about this outbreak are given in the news report above. The microbial etiology is as yet unknown.\n\nCommunity-acquired pneumonia (CAP) can be caused by a variety of microorganisms, including bacteria, viruses, and, less commonly, fungi. Viruses, such as influenza, can cause of outbreaks of CAP. Other viruses that cause CAP in school-aged children include adenovirus, parainfluenza virus, and rhinovirus capable (http://cid.oxfordjournals.org/content/39/5/681.full.pdf). Respiratory syncytial virus and human metapneumovirus are more common in children under 5 years of age (http://reference.medscape.com/medline/abstract/15750086). Common bacterial causes of CAP in this age group include _Mycoplasma pneumoniae_, and _Chlamydia pneumoniae_. Outbreaks of CAP caused by _M. pneumoniae_ occur mostly in crowded environments, like households, schools, college dormitories, and military barracks, when coughing releases small droplets of respiratory secretions into the air that are inhaled by close contacts.\n\nFungi rarely cause pneumonia in otherwise healthy people, but outbreaks of CAP caused by environmental fungi that are characteristic of certain regions of the US, such as _Histoplasma_, _Coccidioides_, and _Blastomyces_, can occasionally occur, when soil harboring these fungi are disturbed. Although unlikely in elementary school children, the opioid epidemic in the US could also cause CAP as a result of aspiration of anaerobic bacterial mouth flora or as a result of injection drug use giving rise to hematogenous _Staphylococcus aureus_ pneumonia.\n\nThe Wheeling Metropolitan Statistical Area, with a population of a 147 950 residents in 2010, consists of 2 counties in the Northern Panhandle of West Virginia and one in eastern Ohio, anchored by the city of Wheeling, which is about 90 miles (about 145 km) southwest of Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wheeling,_West_Virginia_metropolitan_area). A map of showing the location of Wheeling can be found at https://www.google.com/maps/dir/Wheeling,+WV+26003/Pittsburgh,+Pennsylvania.\n\nFurther information on the clinical, microbiologic, and epidemiologic characteristics of this outbreak would be appreciated from knowledgeable sources. - The letter was received about 3:30 p.m. in Henderson Hall, which Arlington Fire officials described as an administrative building. A gunnery sergeant opened a letter and showed it to a superior, a Pentagon official told NBC News.\n\nUp to 11 people began to feel ill, and the building was evacuated. Three of those people were taken to a hospital in stable condition, officials said in a press release. The marines affected reported itchy hands and face and bloody noses, a marine official said. It is unclear how many people suffered from those symptoms.\n\nA large number of police and medics responded to the Northern Virginia military base, which is near the Pentagon and Arlington National Cemetery. The FBI, Naval Criminal Investigative Service (NCIS) and local hazardous material teams cleared the building with base police.\n\nThe NCIS and FBI are conducting a joint investigation, according to a press release. Information was not available immediately on what the unknown substance could be.\n\n[byline: Shomari Stone, Andrea Swalec and Sophia Barnes]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail rapporteur Mary Marshall\n\n******\n[2]\nDate: Wed 28 Feb 2018 8:02 AM ET\nSource: ABC news [edited]\nhttp://abcnews.go.com/US/marines-treated-hazmat-incident-ft-myer-pentagon/story?id=53400402\n\n\nFederal and military officials are investigating a hazmat incident that sickened 11 marines at Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall in Arlington, Virginia, on [Tue 27 Feb 2018]. The FBI and the Naval Criminal Investigative Service were called in when the Marine Corps personnel began feeling ill after an envelope containing an unknown substance was opened at the joint base, which is next to Arlington National Cemetery and near the Pentagon.\n\nPersonnel inside the building were immediately evacuated, officials said, and local fire department hazmat teams responded to the scene within minutes.\n\nA total of 3 marines were transported to a nearby hospital for treatment with non-life threatening conditions. They were treated and released from the hospital late [Tue 27 Feb 2018] night, according to a press release from Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall. The 8 others, who had symptoms ranging from itching to nasal irritation, were being assessed, a marine official told ABC News.\n\nField tests on the suspicious material found inside the envelope came back negative for any known substance, a law enforcement official told ABC News. The envelope and the substance were taken to the FBI's lab at Quantico for further testing. The incident remains under investigation. The FBI and the NCIS are conducting a joint investigation, according to the press release from Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall.\n\nJoint Base Myer-Henderson Hall is the name for the army and marine base commonly-known as Fort Myer, home to the Old Guard honor guard unit and Henderson Hall, where marines are stationed.\n\n[byline: Mark Osborne and Morgan Winsor]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Other reports have indicated there were bloody noses, and burning sensations of the skin. USA: (PA) cause unknown, young adults, 2015-2016, RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=5424985", "date": "2017-11-04 22:29:24", "main_text": "PNEUMONIA - USA: (PENNSYLVANIA) CAUSE UNKNOWN, YOUNG ADULTS, 2015-2016, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n***********************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Thu 2 Nov 2017, 4:53 PM\nSource: Times Online [edited]\nhttp://www.timesonline.com/news/20171102/medexpress-pneumonia-cases-among-young-adults-on-rise\n\n\nMedExpress locations in the 9-county region including Beaver County have been inundated with 74 percent more cases of young adults with pneumonia between 2015 and 2016, and that rising trend is expected to continue.\n\nDiana Burick, a physician's assistant at the MedExpress Center Township office, said college-aged individuals, those ages 18 to 25, are more susceptible to illnesses like pneumonia for variety of reasons. \"You're thinking of folks that live in crowded conditions, like dorms. You're thinking of folks with maybe less than optimal eating habits, less than optimal sleep habits. Folks that maybe aren't practicing the best hand hygiene,\" Burick said. Those who smoke or have asthma also have an increased risk of contracting the flu or pneumonia. Pneumonia is an infection that can cause fluid buildup in the lungs, and in severe cases can cause breathing difficulties.\n\nAccording to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, there were 184 individuals ages 15 to 24 in the United States who died from influenza and pneumonia in 2015, which is a small fraction of the more than 57 000 people who died from influenza and pneumonia among all ages that year.\n\nAnd MedExpress locations in the area have already seen more pneumonia cases this year [2017] than in all of 2016. Symptoms can sometimes vary with pneumonia, and it can evolve from the flu due to a compromised immune system.\n\n\"When you're thinking of the classic symptoms, it's a cough that is persistent, and you're thinking of a fever. Typically a higher fever within that 100-point mark; most folks tend to have that fatigue, that malaise, just not feeling well sensation,\" Burick said. \"At the same point, it's not always isolation of symptoms. Some people are also coming in with those flu-like symptoms.\"\n\nThe most common form of pneumonia is bacterial, meaning it can be treated with antibiotics. But other forms can be viral or fungal, meaning the illness needs to run its course. The most important thing people should be aware of is prevention techniques, Burick said. \"Practicing great hand hygiene, being cautious not to share food or drinks,\" she said. \"It might sound silly, but making sure you're getting adequate sleep and paying attention to your diet.\"\n\n[Byline: Kate Malongowski]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The news report above says that there has been 74 percent more cases of young adults with pneumonia between 2015 and 2016 than previously in a 9-county region that includes Beaver County in the US state of Pennsylvania, but fails to indicate what these counties are or to give the microbial causes for this increase.\n\nCenter Township, a suburban community approximately 25 mi (40 km) northwest of Pittsburgh, is located in Beaver County, Pennsylvania, United States (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_Township,_Beaver_County,_Pennsylvania). Beaver County is on the border with the states of West Virginia and Ohio (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beaver_County,_Pennsylvania#Adjacent_counties) and is part of the Pittsburgh, PA Metropolitan Statistical Area. Adjacent counties are Lawrence (north), Butler (east), Allegheny (southeast), Washington (south), Hancock, West Virginia (west) and Columbiana, Ohio (west).\n\nCommunity-acquired pneumonia (CAP) can be caused by a variety of microorganisms, including bacteria, viruses, and, less commonly, fungi. Common bacterial causes of CAP in the United States are _Streptococcus pneumoniae_ (also called pneumococcus), _Legionella pneumophila_, _Staphylococcus aureus_, _Mycoplasma pneumoniae_, and _Chlamydia pnueumoniae_. Outbreaks of CAP caused by M. pneumoniae occur mostly in crowded environments, like households, schools, college dormitories, and military barracks, when coughing releases small droplets of respiratory secretions into the air that are inhaled by close contacts. The opioid epidemic in the U.S. could also be causing an increase in cases of CAP as a result of aspiration of anaerobic bacterial mouth flora or as a result of injection drug use giving rise to hematogenous _Staphylococcus aureus_ pneumonia.\n\nViruses, such as influenza, also can cause of outbreaks of CAP. Travel-associated pneumonia may be caused by Middle East respiratory syndrome coronavirus (MERS-CoV) indigenous to the Arabian Peninsula or H5N1 or H7N9 strains of avian influenza indigenous to Asia. Fungi rarely cause pneumonia in otherwise healthy people, but outbreaks of CAP caused by environmental fungi that are characteristic of certain regions of the U.S., such as _Histoplasma_, _Coccidioides_ and _Blastomyces_, can occasionally occur, when soil harboring these fungi are disturbed.\n\nFurther information on the clinical, microbiologic, and epidemiologic characteristics of this outbreak would be appreciated from knowledgeable sources. - German tabloid Bild reported that an unknown person sprayed an \"irritating substance\" at people at the check in desk in Terminal 1.\n\nCops reported that the situation was under control but investigations were underway as the cause was \"still unclear\".\n\nFrankfurt Airport's official Twitter account posted in English: \"Fire department operation completed. No more measured values of tear gas can be detected and the affected area is accessible again.\"\n\nFire services were called and the check-in counters were temporarily closed during the incident but have now reopened.\n\nGerman Federal police say that 6 people are being treated for \"light injuries\" relating to their airways.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n******\n[2]\nDate: Mon 11 Sep 2017 11:29 BST\nSource: Daily Mail/Mail Online [edited]\nhttp://tinyurl.com/yalwdptd\n\n\nSix people suffered eye irritation and breathing problems after an unknown person sprayed the check-in area of Frankfurt Airport with a mysterious gas on Monday morning [11 Sep 2017]. Firefighters were called to Terminal 1 after several people reported breathing problems at the check-in counters around 11 am.\n\nThe people were treated at the scene and after no trace of gas was detected the counters were reopened, according to The Local.\n\nThe incident was initially reported by Bild as a gas attack, with the paper saying an unknown assailant had sprayed passengers with a mystery substance.\n\nHowever, it now appears that information was incorrect.\n\nAirport authorities say the exact cause of the incident is still unclear, but investigations are ongoing.\n\nThe check-in area was closed for a short time after the scare, before being reopened around 12.30 pm.\n\nNobody was seriously injured during the incident.\n\n[Byline: Chris Pleasance]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This gas could have been any of a number of irritating gases. Preliminary results indicate a mixture of 2 synthetic opioids, with one of the drugs being consistent with a new fentanyl analogue. There are some reports in the news of this drug being imported from East Asia (I believe it may have 1st surface in Ohio?). Carfentanil is 10 000 times more potent than morphine (100 times more potent than fentanyl). The DEA also released the following statement regarding a rise in carfentanil overdoses/exposures dating back to Sep 2016: https://www.dea.gov/divisions/hq/2016/hq092216.shtml\n\nIf this ultimately is what ends up being identified in the drug analysis, my best suggestion is to contact the local zoo veterinarian, as these drugs have long been used in zoos by veterinarians and intensive and detailed protocols have been written at all institutions using the drug to help guide those who may need to respond to a potential human exposure. The biggest risk in these exposures is re-narcotization, which might explain why the large doses of naloxone were needed.\nI look forward to hearing the results of the testing; please feel free to email with any questions.\n\n--\nKatherine Fogelberg\nUniversity of Tennessee health sciences center\n<Katherine.Fogelberg@unthsc.edu>\n\n******\n[4]\nDate: Thu 8 Jun 2017\nFrom: Ken Waldrup, DVM\n[email address withheld by request]\n\nIn the northern states, they have been having problems with heroin laced with a carfentanil derivative. The legal carfentanil drug is approximately 700 times more potent than heroin so naloxone has a difficult time reversing such a potent opioid. In dealing with large ungulates immobilized with carfentanil, veterinarians learned that naloxone couldn't cut it 30 years ago. Naltrexone is the reversal agent of choice with veterinary use of carfentanil.\n\n--\nKen Waldrup DVM\n[email withheld on request]\n\n******\n[5]\nDate: Jun 9, 2017 2:33 PM\nFrom: \"Powell, Ryan\" <RPowell@rdn.bc.ca>\n\n\nRe: Drug Abuse - USA: (GA) pot. lethal unknown substance, RFI\n\nThe article \"Drug Abuse - USA: (GA) pot. lethal unknown substance, RFI\" resonated with me because of the fentanyl crisis occurring in British Columbia, Canada. Dozens of patients have been hospitalized and there are reports of deaths that may be associated with the drugs, but confirmation is pending.\n\nThe overdoses have been reported over a 48-hour period in Centerville, Perry, Macon-Warner Robins, and Albany, but the drugs may also be sold on the street in other areas of the state. Patients reportedly purchased yellow pills alleged to be Percocet, an opioid pain medication. The substance has not yet been identified but it is extremely potent and has required massive doses of naloxone (Narcan) to counteract its effects. Testing is being done to identify the pills and the ingredients.\n\n1st responders say patients are unconscious or unresponsive and have difficulty breathing or have stopped breathing. Many patients need to be placed on ventilators. Call 9-1-1 immediately if you have taken the pills or if you think someone has used the drug. Opioid overdose is a very dangerous condition that can result in permanent physical and mental damage or even death if medical treatment is not administered right away.\n\nDPH is working closely with the Georgia Bureau of Investigation, Georgia Poison Center and the Georgia Drugs and Narcotics Agency and federal partners on this investigation.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[Purchasing or acquiring drugs from street dealers, even those you think you know, can be a dangerous situation. Mod.AS, edited]\nhttp://www.vetserv.moag.gov.il/Vet/Yechidot/mispo/pirsumim/2017/hodaa_pe_tlafaim.htm\n\n\nOn [Mon 6 Feb 2017], FMD was suspected in a dairy cattle operation in the Western Negev Kibbutz Nir Yitzhak, located approximately 3 km [approx. 1.86 mi] from the Gaza strip border]. FMD has been confirmed by the laboratory; the causative agent has not yet been serotyped.\n\nWe are also informed about clinical signs of FMD in a sheep flock within the Gaza strip. Plausibly, the Nir Yitzhak outbreak originated in the Gaza strip. Since the possibility that an exotic virus strain may be involved has been raised, extreme precaution is prescribed to avoid unnecessary contacts with animals. A 10 km [approx. 6.2 mi] outbreak zone around the affected farm has been implemented [the note includes a table specifying 24 settlements within the 10 km zone. - Mod.AS].\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The described FMD event is exceptional in Israel for the following 2 aspects:\n\n1. Contrary to the disease in small ruminants and beef cattle, FMD has been for decades very rare in Israel's dairy cattle. This is mainly due to their robust immunity maintained throughout the years by a compulsory, methodically, State-applied periodical vaccination regime with polyvalent inactivated vaccines that include regionally circulating virus strains.\n\n2. All reported FMD outbreaks, since the establishment of the State of Israel, are considered to have been introduced from the north (Lebanon, Syria) and (less often) east (Jordan). The current outbreak seems to be the 1st one originating in the south-west. FMD was reported from the Gaza strip in 2012 (serotype SAT2) and 2013 (serotype A); in both cases suspected to have been introduced from Egypt. In both events, the virus did not enter Israel's territory.\n\nFor the location of Nir Yitzhak, which is situated in Israel's \"Hadarom\" (The South) district, see map at http://tinyurl.com/jd8mmq9.\n\nThe (inactivated, oil emulsion) FMD vaccines applied in Israel for the compulsory vaccination of cattle were composed, in 2015, of the following vaccine strains:\n\n1. Serotype O: O Manisa, O-3039, O-4625, O Israel 2007 (4 strains)\n2. Serotype A: A- 4165, A Iran 05 (2 strains)\n3. Serotype Asia 1: Asia1 Shamir (1 vaccine strain).\n\nIt would be interesting to note if the same composition was applied in 2016.\n\nInformation on the serotype and genotype of the causative virus strain involved, the number and age distribution of the affected cattle and the vaccination history of the Nir-Yitzhak dairy operation, is awaited. - Mod.AS\n\nA HealthMap/ProMED-mail map can be accessed at: http://healthmap.org/promed/p/29822.]\nSee Also\n2015\n----\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (03): (HZ) bovine, st O, spread 20151130.3829799\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (02): (HZ) porcine, OIE, st O 20151123.3812972\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel: (HZ) porcine, st. pending, RFI 20151122.3810601\nFoot & mouth disease - Palestinian Auth: (WE) ovine, st O susp, RFI 20151116.3795215\n2014\n----\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (04): (HZ, HM) ovine, st O, genotyping 20140226.2301774\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (03): (HM) ovine, st O, OIE, RFI 20140208.2264193\nFoot & mouth disease - Palestinian Auth: (WE) ovine, caprine, st O, RFI 20140124.2227362\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel (02): (HM) ovine, caprine, RFI 20140116.2177975\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel: (HZ) ovine, caprine, st O 20140114.2170228\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel, PA: st O, genotyping 20140109.2161860\n2013\n----\nFoot & mouth disease - Israel, PA: st. South Korea (06): (SO) WHO, update", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=3805799", "date": "2015-11-20 09:03:48", "main_text": "PNEUMONIA, CAUSE UNKNOWN - SOUTH KOREA (06): (SEOUL) WHO, UPDATE\n****************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Mon 16 Nov 2015\nSource: WHO Emergencies preparedness, response, Disease Outbreak News (DONs) [edited]\nhttp://www.who.int/csr/don/16-november-2015-acute-respiratory-syndrome/en/\n\n\nAcute respiratory syndrome - Republic of Korea\n------------------------------------------------------\nOn 29 Oct 2015, the National IHR Focal Point of the Republic of Korea notified WHO of a cluster of cases with respiratory symptoms in Seoul. Between [19 and 29 Oct 2015], 3 people who work in the same facility developed symptoms of pneumonia. From [22 to 24 Oct 2015], they were admitted to hospital. On [27 Oct 2015], the hospital isolated the patients and alerted local health authorities, which then informed the Korean Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (KCDC).\n\nAdditional information on the outbreak\n-------------------------------------------\nTo date, 84 cases with respiratory symptoms have been identified; 55 of them were diagnosed with pneumonia and 29 cases were mildly symptomatic. The 55 patients with pneumonia were isolated in 7 different hospitals while the 29 patients with mild symptoms were under home quarantine.\n\nAs of [11 Nov 2015], only 1 of the 55 patients with pneumonia was still hospitalized; the other 54 cases had all been discharged. Currently, none of the patients is in critical condition.\n\nPublic health response\n----------------------\nIn response to the outbreak, KCDC and the government of the Republic of Korea have implemented a series of public health measures: issued daily press releases to the public; conducted contact tracing -- 1664 contacts have been monitored on a daily basis; established a hotline for reporting potentially-linked cases; requested hospitals to report pneumonia cases with potential links to the cluster; closed and disinfected the affected facility.\n\nSo far, all PCR tests carried out by the KCDC have been negative, including for adenovirus, respiratory syncytial virus, parainfluenza virus, metapneumovirus, bocavirus, influenza virus, and coronavirus (including MERS-CoV), as well as for _Mycoplasma_, _Chlamydia_, _Corynebacterium_, __Bordetella_, Brucella_, _Coxiella_, and _Legionella_.\n\nAt present, there is no evidence of human-to-human transmission. Investigation on the cause of the outbreak is ongoing.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[So far no etiologic agent has been identified, but we still wait for a full epidemiologic description of the outbreak at Konkuk University School of Veterinary Sciences, which has now involved a total of 84 individuals with respiratory symptoms, 55 of whom had pneumonia and 29 were mildly symptomatic, presumably without pneumonia. - Brucellosis, Q fever, legionellosis shall be reassayed through secondary antibody inspection after 3 weeks.\nIn addition, the test for fungal culture is in progress for 30 suspected patients using the remaining samples after bacteria and virus scan. This may take a few days to few months, and it usually takes 2 to 4 weeks of observation.\nEnvironmental studies: environmental samples were collected from inside the building, which is currently under investigation (started 28 Oct 2015), and it will take about 2 weeks.\nOn the other hand, another 192 students from other departments who entered the building are currently monitored by the KCDC Call Center (109) (a total of 1664).\n* Number of people who are subjected to be monitored: (30 Oct 2015) 964; (31 Oct 2015) 1472; (1 Nov 15) 1664\n87 individuals who are living with the 50 suspected patients are being monitored by public health center for unusual symptoms.\nSo far, unusual cases are not confirmed from the result of monitoring.\n* The system to encourage 527 applicants of the SK Group employment exam to report to the KCDC Call Center (109) is retained.\nKCDC are investigating and taking necessary steps to find the cause and manage the respiratory disease.\nKCDC will actively cooperate with relevant ministries and academic-medical specialists, and will plan to inform the public and the media often.\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The translations were requested of colleagues in Seoul by ProMED-mail consultant, Daniel Lucey, MD of Georgetown University and Jayoung Park. A system for voluntary reporting (109 call center) for adverse symptoms will be in place.\n- Konkuk University Animal Life Science Building (7-story building) is maintaining a state of disinfection and completely controlling access as preventative measures.\n- According to the epidemiology investigation team, the suspected cases have been confirmed to have occurred intensively on the 5th floor laboratory.\n- The building workers, entrants, laboratory workers, and the workers near the laboratory will be classified and examined in detail.\n- KCDC are investigating and taking necessary steps to find the cause and manage the respiratory disease.\n- KCDC will actively cooperate with relevant ministries and academic-medical specialists, and will plan to inform the public and the media often.\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The translations were requested of colleagues in Seoul by ProMED-mail consultant, Daniel Lucey, MD of Georgetown University and Jayoung Park. South Korea: (SO) vet students, RFI", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=3756621", "date": "2015-10-30 22:24:17", "main_text": "PNEUMONIA, CAUSE UNKNOWN - SOUTH KOREA: (SEOUL) VETERINARY STUDENTS, REQUEST FOR INFORMATION\n**************************************************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\n[1]\nDate: Fri 30 Oct 2015\nSource: The Chosun Ilbo [edited]\nhttp://english.chosun.com/site/data/html_dir/2015/10/29/2015102901785.html\n\n\nA mysterious virus has infected 21 graduate students at Konkuk University's school of veterinary science in Seoul. Health authorities have placed all 21 in quarantine and closed off the school building. The Korea Centers for Disease Control and Prevention [KCDC] on Wednesday [28 Oct 2015] said the victims started coming down with pneumonia last week, and a team of epidemiologists have been dispatched to the university.\n\nAccording to the KCDC, those infected are master's and doctoral candidates who used the school's lab from [19 to 28 Oct 2015]. They are being treated in isolation at state-run hospitals.\n\nThe 1st 4 graduate students who showed symptoms were hospitalized at Konkuk University Medical Center and then transferred to the National Medical Center on Wednesday [28 Oct 2015]. All of them visited a cattle fair in Gyeonggi Province last week as well as an animal farm owned by the university in Chungju, North Chungcheong Province.\n\nA university official said they may have contracted brucellosis, which infects cattle and can be transmitted to humans. But some experts suspect Q fever, caused by the _Coxiella burnetii_ bacteria found in the droppings of cattle, swine and sheep. It causes airborne infections among humans. Symptoms such as fever, headache and muscle aches appear after a 2-week gestation period. But Song Dae-sup at Korea University said, \"Brucellosis and Q fever are not commonly found in Korea and are rarely passed on to humans. We need to look at the possibility of pneumonia caused by germs or other toxic agents.\"\n\nLee Jae-gap at Hallym University Medical Center said since only the 4 visited the animal farm, the infection could be mycoplasma pneumonia or whooping cough, which sometimes occur in schools or communities.\n\nKonkuk University sealed off the veterinary school building and told the school's 850 staff and students to report any suspicious symptoms. The building was thoroughly disinfected on Wednesday [28 Oct 2015] morning as well, according to school officials.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This news report was also submitted by Dan Silver, ProMED-mail Rapporteur.]\n\n******\n[2]\nDate: Fri 30 Oct 2015\nSource: The Chosun Ilbo [edited]\nhttp://english.chosun.com/site/data/html_dir/2015/10/30/2015103001031.html\n\n\n10 more graduate students have come down with a mysterious pneumonia attack at Konkuk University's Seoul campus on Thursday [29 Oct 2015], bringing the total to 31.\n\n21 people were diagnosed with the same symptoms earlier. But all have so far tested negative for a dozen well-known infectious diseases.\n\n\"We're still trying to figure out the cause,\" a spokesman for the Korea Centers for Disease Control and Prevention [KCDC] said Thursday.\n\nStudents look at instructions in front of a makeshift clinic at Konkuk University in Seoul on Thursday [29 Oct 2015]. The school said all patients are graduate students at the school of veterinary science and most have mild symptoms.\n\n23 are in isolation at state-run hospitals, while 8 with very mild symptoms are quarantined at home. All have tested negative for brucellosis, Q fever, and _Legionella_, which were among the prime suspects of the mysterious infection. They also tested negative for bacterial diseases like _Mycoplasma_ and _Chlamydia_ and viruses like Middle East respiratory syndrome [MERS] and flu.\n\nMeanwhile, it has emerged that the SK Group conducted recruitment exams on the campus last Sunday [25 Oct 2015], when the outbreak was probably already underway. Authorities asked 500 people who took the exams to report to the KCDC if they have symptoms like high fever.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This news report was also submitted by Dan Silver, ProMED-mail Rapporteur.]\n\n[The fact that a large group of veterinary graduate students became ill with pneumonia over a short period of time suggests a point source outbreak, i.e., they were all exposed to the same source over a brief time. The development of additional cases over time and geographic areas will be very useful in determining whether the cases are related to a point source.\n\nWe are not told exactly the severity of the illness, but almost 75 percent of cases were ill enough to require hospitalization. The fact that the illness seems at the present time to be limited to graduate veterinary students suggests a zoonosis. Brucellosis, Q fever, MERS, and influenza, as well as legionellosis, chlamydiosis, and _Mycoplasma_ infection were said to have been ruled out, but the report does not mention SARS. I don't know how legionellosis was ruled out, but Pontiac fever, a non-pneumonic form of legionellosis, occurs as a point source outbreak with high attack rates following exposure to aerosolized _Legionella_. Pontiac fever is diagnosed serologically; culture and legionella urinary antigen are usually negative. However, the severity of the Pontiac fever is so mild that it usually does require hospitalization. Other etiologies to be considered should include psittacosis (again I am unsure how a chlamydial infection was ruled out), tularemia, pneumonic plague, and anthrax. Histoplasmosis, although very rare in South Korea, can also cause a point source outbreak of an acute respiratory illness. More information is obviously needed from knowledgeable sources to develop a list of potential etiologies.\n\nKonkuk University is a private university located in Seoul and Chungju. Gyeonggi Province surrounds Seoul. Chungju is a city in North Chungcheong Province, which is southeast of Seoul. virulence unknown", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=3375592", "date": "2015-05-20 18:03:29", "main_text": "AVIAN INFLUENZA, HUMAN (106): NOVEL VIRUSES, VIRULENCE UNKNOWN\n**************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Tue 19 May 2015\nSource: Reuters [edited]\nhttp://www.reuters.com/article/2015/05/19/us-health-birdflu-oie-idUSKBN0O41NX20150519\n\n\nMore than 35 countries have been hit in a surge in bird flu outbreaks since early [2014], killing tens of millions of poultry, the World Organisation for Animal Health (OIE) said on Tue 19 May 2015.\n\nUS poultry and egg producers have been grappling with a record outbreak of an avian flu, mainly the H5N2 strain, that has led to the culling of more than 33 million birds since December 2014 and is now threatening supplies of poultry.\n\nHighly pathogenic H5N8, which like H5N2 has not been found in humans, was also reported in a few US states, according to the US Department of Agriculture. The H5N8 strain was discovered early in 2014 in Korea and China, and reached Japan soon afterwards. \"From there the strain probably spread with migratory wild birds to India, Europe, Canada and later the United States of America,\" the OIE said in its statement.\n\nThe Paris-based organisation [OIE] urged its 180 member countries to better apply biosecurity measures in farms, live bird markets and in trade, and step up surveillance to curb the spread of the disease. The OIE data shows 28 countries were hit by outbreaks of the highly pathogenic H5 and H7 [antigenic] types of bird flu since the start of 2015, up from 19 countries affected in 2014 and 14 countries in 2013.\n\nA global epizootic -- an epidemic outbreak in animals -- of H5N1 bird flu, which emerged in early 2004, led to several cases in humans, of which more than half proved fatal. It also led to the death of tens of million poultry, OIE said. Although a pandemic was averted, the H5N1 strain is still present. Several outbreaks have been confirmed in West African countries in recent months, and the epidemic continues in Egypt, in Israel and the Palestinian territories.\n\n[byline: reporting by Sybille de La Hamaide; editing by Raissa Kasolowsky]\n\n--\ncommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[A subscriber who wishes to remain anonymous also points out, \"Other articles on this topic report that serological evidence of human infections with various H5N2 viruses have been detected in Taiwan (2012), South Africa (2011), and Japan (2005-2006). unknown", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=2986454", "date": "2014-11-24 20:55:37", "main_text": "PRION DISEASE UPDATE (07): ORIGIN OF FOURTH US VCJD CASE STILL UNKNOWN\n**********************************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Tue 7 Oct 2014 [updated, original announcement dated 2 Jun 2014]\nSource: Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC) and Texas Department of State Health Services [edited]\nhttp://www.cdc.gov/ncidod/dvrd/vcjd/other/confirmed-case-in-texas.htm\n\n\nThe CDC and the Texas Department of State Health Services (DSHS) have completed the investigation of the recently reported 4th vCJD case in the United States. It confirmed that the case was in a US citizen born outside the Americas and indicated that the patient's exposure to the BSE/vCJD agent most likely occurred before he moved to the United States; the patient had resided in Kuwait, Russia and Lebanon.\n\nThe completed investigation did not support the patient's having had extended travel to European countries, including the United Kingdom, or travel to Saudi Arabia. The specific overseas country where this patient's infection [could have] occurred is less clear, largely because the investigation did not definitely link him to a country where other known vCJD cases likely had been infected.\n\nVariant Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease (vCJD), 1st described in 1996 in the United Kingdom, is a rare, degenerative, fatal brain disorder in humans. It is believed to be caused by consumption of products from cows with the disease bovine spongiform encephalopathy (BSE, or \"mad cow\" disease). Worldwide, more than 220 variant CJD patients have been reported, with a majority of them in the United Kingdom (177 cases) and France (27 cases).\n\nThis case is the 4th to be reported in the United States. In each of the 3 previous cases, infection likely occurred outside the United States, including the United Kingdom (2 cases) and Saudi Arabia (1 case). The history of this 4th patient, including extensive travel to Europe and the Middle East, supports the likelihood that infection occurred outside the United States. CDC assisted the Texas Department of State Health Services' (DSHS) investigation of this case and has continued to establish the patient's history, including the potential source of infection.\n\nThe classic form of CJD, which is not caused by the BSE agent, occurs worldwide, including in the United States. Annually, for every one million people in the United States, 1-2 develop classic CJD.\n\nMore information about variant CJD, including how it differs from classic CJD, is available in the Variant Creutzfeldt-Jakob Disease Fact Sheet (http://www.cdc.gov/ncidod/dvrd/vcjd/factsheet_nvcjd.htm).\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nTerry S. COLI EHEC - UK (16): UNKNOWN SOURCE\n**************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\nhttp://www.promedmail.org\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\nhttp://www.isid.org\n\nDate: Wed 5 Nov 2014\nSource: Public Health England (PHE) [edited]\nhttps://www.gov.uk/government/news/phe-investigating-national-outbreak-of-e-coli\n\n\nSo far 75 people have been affected (primary cases): 67 in England, 3 in Wales and 5 in Scotland [by _E. coli_]. Genetic analysis has shown that all these individuals have all been infected with the same strain. Most of these cases are adults but the total number of cases has an age range of between 2 to 90. 27 males and 48 (64 percent) females have been affected. In addition, there have also been 10 secondary cases reported. These are people who have become unwell through contact with a primary case.\n\nFurther details are available on 82 of the total cases all of whom reported symptoms of diarrhea. Bloody diarrhea was reported by 58 people (71 percent) and 25 people have been hospitalized as a result of their illness. There have been no deaths or cases of hemolytic-uremic syndrome which is a serious complication of an _E. coli_ infection which can result in kidney failure.\n\nPHE is working with Public Health Wales, Health Protection Scotland, Animal and Plant Health Agency and the Food Standards Agency to gather, share and analyse information. At present there is no clear indication as to what is causing the outbreak.\n\nDr Bob Adak, head of the gastrointestinal diseases department at PHE, said: \"Any infection with _E. coli_ can be very serious. We have carried out initial investigations which involved interviewing some of the affected people to look for connections that link individuals in terms of the foods that they had eaten and the places they had visited in the days before they became ill. This information is now being used to develop more in-depth investigations designed to identify the cause of the outbreak.\"\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[The posting does not specifically state that the pathogen is _E. coli_ O157 or any other enterohemorrhagic strain, but the context of the article strongly suggests it. The Departments of Meurthe-et-Moselle and Moselle seem particularly concerned. \"The GDS [National Federation of Animal Health Protection Groups] and veterinary practitioners have developed a framework for investigations in cooperation with Prof Schelcher, Veterinary School, Toulouse.\n\nThe phenomenon has been observed since the beginning of the lambing season. On 14 Dec 2012, GDS Meurthe-et-Moselle identified agalactia in 15 out of a total of about 200 farms. Affected farms were visited, the attack rate of the lambing ewes was recorded as 50 to 100 percent. The reported cases appear scattered in the departments concerned, demonstrating absence of colostrum/milk during the 1st post-parturition days. This leads to the need to hand-feed the lambs. Lactation appears again (with or without therapeutic treatment) in the ewes 2-8 days post parturition.\n\nNo particular clinical symptoms have been seen in the ewes prior to the observed compromised lactation.\n\nThe established platform of investigation applies to veterinarians and farmers in other geographical regions to report similar observations to a given e-mail address (see source url).\n\n[Byline: Michel Jeanney]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[This is not a case of the infectious mycoplasma disease in sheep and goats called \"contagious agalactiae\", which, on top of its effect upon lactation, also causes ocular and joints (arthritic) changes.\n\nUpdated results of the surveillance and of the epidemiological investigation are anticipated with interest. According to this report, the Israeli, who recently arrived in China after travelling [in] India, contacted an Israeli businessman a few days ago and told him he was feeling ill, was suffering from severe back pain, had difficulty drinking and was vomiting constantly.\n\nThe businessman rushed the Israeli to a local hospital where he underwent a cardiac catheterization procedure. While at the hospital the Israeli suffered from hallucinations during which he claimed the Chinese doctors were trying to harvest his organs.\n\nThe physicians initially thought the man was suffering from some sort of mental illness and tried to determine whether he used drugs. Some doctors suggested transferring the Israeli to a psychiatric hospital after he recuperated, but his condition quickly deteriorated. He slipped in and out of consciousness, and the doctors hooked him up to a ventilator.\n\nThe mystery was solved when an infectious disease specialist was rushed to the Israeli's room and determined that he had contracted rabies. It remains unclear whether the Israeli, who died on Wed 19 Sep 2012, [had been] bitten by a dog and if so when [and where].\n\nMore than 55 000 people dies of rabies each year, [many] in India.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap alerts\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n\n[People contract rabies predominantly following a deep bite or scratch by an infected animal. Dogs are the main host and transmitter of rabies in Asia. The initial symptoms of rabies are fever and often pain or an unusual or unexplained tingling, pricking or burning sensation (paraesthesia) at the wound site. As the virus spreads through the central nervous system, progressive, fatal inflammation of the brain and spinal cord develops. 2 forms of the disease can follow. People with furious rabies exhibit signs of hyperactivity, excited behaviour, hydrophobia and sometimes aerophobia. After a few days, death occurs by cardio-respiratory arrest. Paralytic rabies accounts for about 30 percent of the total number of human cases.\n\nNo tests are available to diagnose rabies infection in humans before the onset of clinical disease, and unless the rabies-specific signs of hydrophobia or aerophobia are present, the clinical diagnosis may be difficult. Human rabies can be confirmed intra-vitam and post mortem by various diagnostic techniques aimed at detecting whole virus, viral antigens or nucleic acids in infected tissues (brain, skin, urine or saliva). [See: http://www.who.int/mediacentre/factsheets/fs099/en/index.html].\n\nThe preceding press report does not identify the type of test used to establish the diagnosis. The incubation period for rabies virus infection in humans is typically 1-3 months, but may range from less than one week to more than one year, depending among other things on on the site and size of the initial wound. The report lacks information on the date of arrival of the patient in Beijing or the length of his stay India [or elsewhere]. Hence it cannot be determined whether he contracted infection prior to or after his arrival in Beijing. It is also possible that he may have been infected elsewhere (possibly even in Israel) prior to his arrival in India. COLI 0157 - USA: (OHIO, MICHIGAN), UNKNOWN SOURCE\n****************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Tue 24 Jun 2008\nSource: RedOrbit, The Columbus Dispatch (Ohio) report [edited]\n<http://www.redorbit.com/news/health/1447268/e_coli_cases_reach_16_in_central_ohio_1_source/>\n\n\nCentral Ohio health officials added another case of _E. coli_ O157:H7\nillness yesterday [23 Jun 2008], bringing the tally for the outbreak\nin Delaware, Fairfield, and Franklin counties to 16. Corr.ATS, edited]\n<http://www.nr2.ru/crimea/169789.html>\n\n\nThe sailors who suffered on the ship \"Roksolana\" are going to sue the\nowner of the ship. Their interests will be represented by the Kerch\nUnion of trade and fishing sailors.\n\nAccording to the representative of the Union, the situation on\n\"Roksolana\" is a repetition of the story on \"Odysk\". Moreover, the\nship has the same structure as the \"Odysk\", and in both ships the\nilluminators [windows] of the crewmembers open to the corridor and\nnot to the outside.\n\nThe preliminary information is that the gas came from the cargo section.\n\nThe sailors asked the Union to represent them as they consider that\nthe contract they signed does not provide fair compensation.\n\nLet's remember that after the previous incident with the ship \"Odysk\",\nthe sailors received USD 10 000 each and the families of the deceased\nreceived USD 50 000, twice the amount stated in the contracts.\n\nAccording to \"Noviy Region\" the ship \"Roksolana\" sailed under the\nflag of Belize with 11 crewmembers on board and carrying 1641 tons of\ngrain. On the morning of 16 Mar 2008, the captain of the ship asked\nfor help after he found a dead sailor and 4 others poisoned. After\nthe evacuation of the crew, the members of the group for radiation\nand chemical protection took samples of the air from the ship's\ninterior. The concentration of poisonous agents in the air was 200\ntimes higher than the safety limit. The specialists stated that it\nwas poisoning with phosphine. The ship had been treated with\n[fumigating agents] against insects and rats. It is the 3rd case of\nthe same kind on the Crimean coast.\n\n[Byline: Anna Marikhu]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail Correspondents ATS/VM\n\n[The reported case is the 3rd after a planned treatment of the ships\nwith fumigating agents. This kind of work needs careful safety\nprocedures and proper instruction. The ship owners have to provide\nspecial protective outerwear and respiratory equipment for\nanti-rodent treatment. - Corr.VM\n\nPhosphine gas is frequently used in the grain industry for fumigating\ngrain, especially grains that are held for any period of time. The\nfumigation decreases weevils and rodents preying on the grain.\n\nPhosphine gas is a colorless, inflammable gas with carbide or\nfish-like odor and some describe it as a garlic-like odor. It is most\nfrequently toxic by inhalation. The amount that is toxic is relative\nto the species inhaling it. The amount per cubic meter and the length\nof time of exposure govern the toxicity. The higher the amount means\nthe lower the time necessary to cause toxicity and conversely, the\nlower the amount per cubic meter the longer the time of exposure\nrequired to produce intoxication. The levels are not cumulative.\n\nPhosphine is most often sold in the form of aluminium phosphide,\ncalcium phosphide, or zinc phosphide pellets. Phosphine is released\nwhen it encounters moisture, such as atmospheric moisture or gastric\nacid in the stomach of rodents.\n\nIf the crew believed there were fish on board then they may not have\nthought a fishy odor to be odd. However, with the grain off-gassing\nin the ship's hold and no outside ventilation for the crew, this was\na set up for a deadly situation.\n\nPhosphine is a very toxic gas, and is also generated as a by-product\nduring the manufacturing of methamphetamine. - Mod.TG]\nSee Also\nPoisoning, agent unknown - Ukraine: (Yalta) 20080321.1081\n2007\n----\nPhosphine, fatal - Ukraine (Yalta) 20070114.0189\n........................................tg/mj/jw\n*##########################################################*\n************************************************************\nProMED-mail makes every effort to verify the reports that\nare posted, but the accuracy and completeness of the\ninformation, and of any statements or opinions based\nthereon, are not guaranteed. Despite a great deal\nof research on the physiology, reproductive biology, and diet of\npandas in the wild and in captivity, there is little information on\nwild panda mortality. Here, we integrate previously unavailable data\non mortality of wild pandas. We report 3 recent phases of panda\nmortality: deaths due to bamboo flowering in the 1970s and 1980s;\nsurprisingly extensive poaching in the 1980s and 1990s; and the\ngrowing importance of a parasitic infection over the past few years.\nOur analyses suggest that the current most significant threat to wild\npanda survival is disease due to extra-intestinal migration (visceral\nlarva migrans) of an ascarid nematode. We demonstrate that the\nprobability of death of wild pandas being caused by this disease\nincreased significantly between 1971 and 2006 and discuss the\npossible factors leading to the emergence of this disease.\n\n[Jin-Shuo Zhang (1,2), Peter Daszak (3), Hua-Li Huang (4), Guang-You\nYang (5), A. Marm Kilpatrick (3), and Shu-Yi Zhang (2)\n\n1. Institute of Zoology and Graduate University, Chinese Academy of\nSciences, Beijing, 100080, China\n2. School of Life Science, East China Normal University, Shanghai,\n200062, China.\n3. The Consortium for Conservation Medicine, New York, NY 10001, USA\n4. Baishuijiang Nature Reserve, Wenxian, Gansu, 746400, China\n5. Sichuan Agricultural University, Ya'an, Sichuan, 625014, China]\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nDr Peter Daszak\nExecutive Director,\nConsortium for Conservation Medicine,\nNew York, NY 10001\nUSA\n<daszak@conservationmedicine.org>\n\n[We are grateful to Dr Daszak, one of the authors, for providing the\nabstract above with his following comments:\n\n\"Further to the posting about unknown illnesses in giant pandas, I\nwanted to alert you to an upcoming article in the journal EcoHealth,\nwhich supports the comments of Dr Karesh, that infectious diseases\nhave been reported from pandas in the past, and are perhaps\nsurprisingly important as a cause of death in wild pandas. The\narticle is in press, and will appear in the March 2008 edition of\nEcoHealth (a Springer Journal, <http://www.ecohealth.net/>), but will\nlikely appear online during January or February (2008). In the spirit\nof ProMED-mail as the key early reporter of emerging disease issues,\nhere is the abstract -- please feel free to post this information on\nProMED\". - Mod.AS]\n\n[This is welcome information and serves both as a reminder of the\nvarious factors that can affect wildlife population dynamics, and\nalso as a great example of how important health information can\nquickly flow from a scientific meeting via ProMED-mail to a global\naudience and be confirmed (or corrected) long before the information\nis available via traditional journal publication.\n\n--\nWilliam B. Karesh, D.V.M.\nCo-chair, IUCN Species Survival Commission - Wildlife Health Specialist\nGroup\nDirector, Field Veterinary Program\nWildlife Conservation Society\n2300 Southern Blvd.\nBronx, NY 10460 U.S.A.\n<wkaresh@wcs.org>]\nSee Also\nUnknown illness, giant pandas - China (03) 20071118.3732\nUnknown illness, giant pandas - China (02) 20071115.3709\nUnknown illness, giant pandas - China: RFI 20071114.3691\n...................................mhj/arn/mj/lm\n\n*##########################################################*\n************************************************************\nProMED-mail makes every effort to verify the reports that\nare posted, but the accuracy and completeness of the\ninformation, and of any statements or opinions based\nthereon, are not guaranteed. China (03)", "url": "https://promedmail.org/promed-post/?id=37850", "date": "2007-11-18 18:00:12", "main_text": "UNKNOWN ILLNESS, GIANT PANDAS - CHINA (03)\n******************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\n\nDate: Fri 16 Nov 2007\nSource: China Daily [edited]\n<http://www.chinadaily.com.cn/china/2007-11/16/content_6259208.htm>\n\n\nThis year's [2007] outbreak of contagious diseases among giant pandas\nhas emphasized the need for more measures to ensure the bears' future\nsafety, delegates to the 18th Annual Conference of the Chinese\nCommittee of Breeding Techniques for the Giant Panda have said.\n\nZhang Zhihe, the committee's chairman, said to avoid possible future\noutbreaks of highly infectious diseases, such as SARS (severe acute\nrespiratory syndrome) and bird flu, it is critical to do more\nresearch on the supervision, prevention and treatment of such\nconditions -- as well as so far undiagnosed diseases -- and establish\nan emergency response system.\n\nGiant pandas have been forced to move from a mountainous area of\nsouthwestern China due to food shortages, as their bamboo food\nflowers and dies as part of a natural cycle, an animal expert said.\n\nSpeaking at the 5-day conference, which ended Thursday [15 Nov 2007]\nin the Sichuan provincial capital, Yang Xuyu, deputy chief of Sichuan\nWildlife Management Station, said about 20 panda cubs are bred in\ncaptivity every year in China. But if the bears live together in\nconfined spaces, contagious diseases can quickly spread.\n\nA delegate who asked not to be named said 10 pandas at the Wolong\nNature Reserve this year [2007] became infected with a rare\ncontagious disease from which 2 of them later died [Could the nature\nof the suspected \"rare\" disease be specified? Clinical signs,\nlaboratory tests etc. will be helpful. - Mod.AS].\n\nVets from the Chengdu Research Base of Giant Panda Breeding, where\nZhang is based, worked with staff from Wolong to treat the sick\npandas but failed to diagnose the ailment, he said.\n\nYang said that in an effort to prevent the spread of potentially\nfatal diseases, additional enclosures for the bears will be built at\nboth Chengdu and Wolong.\n\nThe State Forestry Administration recently gave Wolong 20 million\nyuan [USD 2.7 million] to build 40 new dens some 20 km from its\nexisting ones. The Chengdu base is currently considering possible\nsites for its new compounds, he said.\n\nYang also warned of the danger of bamboo flowering, which, since\n2005, has expanded to an area of 24 000 hectares in Sichuan, about\n1.4 percent of the edible bamboo in the province, he told China Daily.\n\nNine varieties of bamboo have been seen flowering, which account for\nabout 30 percent of the varieties eaten by pandas.\n\nIn the 1980s, in the mountainous regions of Sichuan, extensive\nblossoming of the arrow bamboo -- the pandas' favorite -- led to many\nbears dying of disease and starvation, Yang said.\n\nThis year [2007], to avoid a recurrence, the Sichuan provincial\nforestry bureau has developed an emergency response plan and asked\nlocal forestry bureaus to implement it in the event of extensive\nblossoming.\n\nYang said that if 15 percent of the total bamboo area or 100 percent\nof a single variety is found to be flowering, all bears in that area\nwill be inoculated and/or relocated to ensure their safety.\n\nOften referred to as living fossils, giant pandas are found mainly in\nSichuan, which is home to about 1200 of them, or 76 percent of the\ncountry's total.\n\nMore than 80 officials and experts from animal protection\norganizations in 8 countries attended this year's [2007] conference.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail Rapporteur Dan Silver\n\n[For Bill Karesh's commentary, see 20071114.3691. - Mod.AS]\nSee Also\nUnknown illness, giant pandas - China (02) 20071115.3709\nUnknown illness, giant pandas - China: RFI 20071114.3691\n.............................................arn/msp/lm\n\n\n*##########################################################*\n************************************************************\nProMED-mail makes every effort to verify the reports that\nare posted, but the accuracy and completeness of the\ninformation, and of any statements or opinions based\nthereon, are not guaranteed. Pandas\nare being forced to move form their normal locations in search of\nfood because at present the bamboo is flowering. Rappt.DS, edited]\n<http://news.sina.com.cn/o/2007-11-12/114512888303s.shtml>\n\n\nAt the opening of the 18th Annual Conference of the Chinese Committee\nof Breeding Techniques for Giant Pandas in Chengdu, Sichuan,\nresearcher Zhihe Zhang, director of the Committee, presented this\nyear's [2007] Committee work report to the conference.\n\nIt was stated at the conference that there has been an outbreak of an\nunknown infectious disease among pandas in some nature reserves and\nprotective units in China this year [2007]. The health and safety of\nthe captive and wild giant panda species has therefore become a key\nissue at this year's conference.\n\n\"Small scale outbreak[s] of disease this year [2007] in China alert\nus to the need to pay active attention to the safety of the [giant\npanda] population.\" Zhihe Zhang stated that population safety is one\nof the most important issues affecting the survival of the giant\npanda. To avoid the emergence of vicious infectious diseases similar\nto SARS [severe acute respiratory syndrome] or avian influenza in the\ngiant panda population, it is extremely important to immediately\nstrengthen monitoring, prevention, and treatment/research of canine\ndistemper virus and other known and unknown infectious diseases. It\nis also extremely urgent to organize response teams, equipment, and\nemergency systems.\n\n--\nCommunicated by:\nProMED-mail Rapporteur Dan Silver\n\n[ProMED-mail has heard little regarding disease in giant pandas and\nhas referred this story to William Karesh of the Wildlife\nConservation Society for further comment. - Ed.LM]\n\n[Unfortunately, the news report provides little for interpretation.\nIf indeed the problems being mentioned are due to an infectious\ndisease, there are quite a few that have been reported over the years\nthat can infect giant pandas. Serological evidence of exposure to\ncanine viruses such as morbillivirus, adenovirus, parvovirus, and\ncoronavirus has been reported. Of course, test validation for pandas\nis unlikely and the possibility of cross-reaction to related viruses\nis quite possible. Bacterial septicemias due to _E. coli_ have been\nreported in captive pandas also.\n\nGiven the behavioral ecology (mostly solitary animals except during\nan extremely brief breeding season and living at low densities)\ncontact rates among wild pandas would be very low. Though not\nimpossible, it would seem unlikely that that same infectious agent\nwas spreading among pandas unless it had an extremely long incubation\nand/or period of shedding and not rapidly fatal. More likely is that\nthey are being exposed to organisms from other species, including\ndomestic animals that may be contaminating the limited remaining\npanda habitat, which may lead to cross-species transmission of the\nagents. Non-infectious causes such as environmental contaminants\nshould not be completely discounted either.\n\nPossibly, the more valuable piece of information in this news report\nis the official recognition for the need for better surveillance and\nresponse teams to investigate morbidity and mortality. If coordinated\nwith local domestic animal health monitoring or reporting systems\naround protected areas, it may shed light on prevalence of a number\nof diseases and sources of infection.\n\nWilliam B. COLI O157, UNKNOWN SOURCE - AUSTRALIA (SOUTH AUSTRALIA)\n**********************************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\nDate: Tue 13 Feb 2007\nFrom: ProMED-mail <promed@promedmail.org>\nSource: Adelaide Now [edited]\n<http://www.news.com.au/adelaidenow/story/0,22606,21222831-5006301,00.html>\n\nThe source of a spate of _E. coli_ [O157] infections across South\nAustralia (SA) remains a mystery as authorities yesterday, 12 Feb\n2007, admitted they were not confident of finding the cause.\nPublic health director Dr. Kevin Buckett said finding the origin of\nthe potentially fatal bacteria was proving to be an uphill battle.\n\"We're not overly confident but we're working very hard to track it\n(the cause) down,\" Dr. Buckett said. \"We'll keep pursuing it as far\nas we can.\"\nThe admission came as the Health Department confirmed 3 new cases of\n_E. coli_ infection. There have now been 10 cases reported in 2007,\nwhich is more than a quarter of the average yearly total.\n\"Here in SA, we get around 30 to 40 cases of all strains of _E. coli_\neach year,\" he said. \"These cases are usually quite sporadic and\noccur throughout the year. \"When we get a lot of cases occurring at\nonce and they seem to be linked in some way, then I guess we call\nthis an outbreak,\" Dr. Buckett said.\nHe said the fact that the infected people lived in different areas --\nincluding one in regional SA -- and were aged between 2 and 81 years\nof age, made identifying common links difficult.\nFlinders University gastroenterologist Professor Graeme Young said\nfinding the cause of the outbreak would involve a degree of\n\"detective work\". \"I think that if there isn't a common factor\nbetween the people, it makes it very hard to understand why this is\nhappening,\" Professor Young said.\n[Byline: Jessica Leo]\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\nSee Also\nHemolytic uremic syndrome - Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\nDate: 20 Sep 2006\nFrom: ProMED-mail <promed@promedmail.org>\nSource: AP via NY Times [edited]\n<http://www.nytimes.com/aponline/world/AP-India-Dying-Lions.html?_r=1&oref=slogin>\n\nMystery Disease Killing Lions in India\n-------------------------------------------\nNearly 2 dozen crossbred lions are slowly dying in northern India\nfrom a mysterious disease afflicting the hybrid offspring of Asiatic\nand African cats paired in a discontinued experimental program.\nZookeepers are mournfully watching the results of the program, which\nbegan in the late 1980s at the Chhatbir Zoo and was ended in 2002,\nafter many of the nearly 80 crossbred lions were struck by a\nmysterious disease linked to inbreeding and a weakened gene pool,\nsaid Kuldip Kumar, Punjab state's conservator of forests and wildlife.\nWildlife officials had originally hoped the hybrid cats could be\nintroduced into the wild in an effort to bolster India's endangered\nwild lion population.\nWhen the program ended, all of the male lions were given vasectomies\nto prevent further breeding, Kumar said.\nIndian wildlife laws prohibit killing the animals.\nIt will take about 6 years for the remaining 22 crossbred lions to\ndie of natural causes, Kumar said.\nZoo authorities have decided to launch a new captive breeding project\nusing \"pure Asiatic lion stock from other zoos in the country, but\nonly after the last of the earlier crop of lions have been phased\nout,\" he said.\nThe zoo has recently built an enclosed area for the oldest and most\ninfirm of the lions so they are not attacked by the more robust cats.\n\"At any time, the zoo has around 4 to 5 lions that are too old and\nweak to compete with the younger, more aggressive lions,\" Kumar said.\nThe lions are fed boneless meat, he said.\nWildlife experts say rampant poaching is driving the Asiatic lion to\nextinction, especially in the Gir forests in western India, the last\nwild refuge of the big cats.\nThe last lion census conducted in the forests in 2000 put the number\nof Asiatic lions at 320. The animals' numbers have further dwindled\ndue to poaching, open wells that act as death traps and human\nencroachment on lion habitat.\nLions are killed for their pelts and claws, both of which command a\nhuge price in the illegal wildlife trade.\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[Is the progeny suffering from a lethal genetic disease or from a\ngenetic susceptibility to a prevailing infectious disease?\nMore information on the outcome of this, clearly unsuccessful\nbreeding project, is anticipated. - Mod.AS]\n.............lm/mpp/arn/msp/mpp\n*##########################################################*\n************************************************************\nProMED-mail makes every effort to verify the reports that\nare posted, but the accuracy and completeness of the\ninformation, and of any statements or opinions based\nthereon, are not guaranteed. COLI O157 - USA (MULTISTATE): UNKNOWN SOURCE\n***********************************************\nA ProMED-mail post\n<http://www.promedmail.org>\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n<http://www.isid.org>\nDate: Fri 7 Apr 2006\nFrom: ProMED-mail <promed@promedmail.org>\nSource: FoodConsumer.org [edited]\n<http://www.foodconsumer.org/777/8/FSIS_Reminds_Consumers_to_Properly_Handle_and_Cook_Ground_Beef_Products_.shtml>\n\nFSIS: Handle ground beef products properly\n-----------------------------------------------\nThe USA Department of Agriculture's Food Safety and Inspection\nService (FSIS) is issuing a public health alert to remind consumers\nto ensure that meat products are fully cooked and properly handled\nbefore they are consumed.\nFSIS has received reports of 14 illnesses caused by _E. coli_ O157:H7\nwith matching microbiological profiles. There is no link to a\nspecific product, but illnesses from this pathogen can be associated\nwith consumption of raw or undercooked ground beef. Illnesses have\nbeen found in California, Iowa, New York, Ohio, Michigan, Rhode\nIsland and Wisconsin. These illnesses occurred over a 6-month period,\nbeginning in September 2005 through March 2006, and FSIS is working\nclosely with State and local health officials to determine the\nexposure that led to illness.\nTherefore, FSIS wants to remind all consumers of the proper handling\nand cooking of meat products. Safe steps in food handling, cooking,\nand storage are essential to prevent foodborne illness. Consumers\nshould follow the 4 guidelines to keep food safe:\n1. Clean: Wash hands and surfaces often. Wash your hands with warm,\nsoapy water for 20 seconds before and after handling food. Wash your\ncutting boards, dishes, etc. with hot, soapy water after preparing\neach food item. Wash fruits and vegetables with cold water before\nusing. There is no need to wash or rinse meat or poultry.\n2. Separate: Don't cross-contaminate. Separate raw, cooked, and\nready-to-eat foods while shopping, preparing, or storing. Never place\ncooked food on a plate which previously held raw meat, poultry, or\nseafood.\n3. Cook: Cook food to proper temperatures. To be sure bacteria and\npathogens are destroyed, cook ground beef products to 160 F. Use a\nfood thermometer to be sure!\n4. Chill: Refrigerate promptly. Refrigerate or freeze perishables,\nprepared foods, and leftovers within 2 hours or sooner.\n--\nProMED-mail\n<promed@promedmail.org>\n[Matching microbiological profiles (presumably genetic matches)\noccurring over 6 months and scattered across the USA suggest a common\nreservoir that is nonperishable, such as frozen ground beef rather\nthan unpasteurized milk or produce.
